24:595:51891:27:28:72:543:285:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:find weaker or no results. This is the fourth set of additional analyses whose results are reported 
24:596:51991:28:37:72:183:257:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:in Panel C of Table V. 
24:597:52014:37:28:90:543:220:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:If we define industry IPO waves by simply grouping IPOs in the same industry and the same 
24:598:52104:28:28:72:543:192:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:calendar year and repeat our portfolio formation procedures and calendar-time trading strategies, 
24:599:52202:28:27:72:542:164:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:we find a much weaker underperformance among low-BM-low-GM stocks. Under such a pseudo 
24:600:52289:27:28:72:547:137:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:industry IPO wave definition, low-BM-low -GM IPO stocks underperform less than 30 bps per 
24:601:52379:28:28:72:543:109:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:month, a significant drop from 103 bps per month in the case where we use a more  precise 
24:602:52469:28:0:72:543:81:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:procedure to identify industry IPO waves (Table IV, Panel A). Moreover, when we repeat our 
25:603:52563:0:28:72:543:709:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:portfolio formation procedures and calendar-time trading strategies for all CRSP/COMPUSTAT 
25:604:52654:28:28:72:547:681:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:stocks, the underperformance of low-BM-low -GM stocks becomes economically insignificant, at 
25:605:52747:28:37:72:191:653:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:a mere 6 bps per month. 
25:606:52771:37:28:90:543:616:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Overall, using both event-time and calendar-time analyses, we find strong empirical support 
25:607:52863:28:27:72:543:588:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:for  our  hypothesis  that  low-margin-induced  high  initial  sales  growth  fuels  optimism  among 
25:608:52964:27:28:72:543:561:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:investors, resulting in overpricing of some growth firms in the initial growth stage of their life 
25:609:53063:28:28:72:543:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:cycle and leading to the long-run underperformance of these firms. We find that this key result is 
25:610:53162:28:27:72:543:505:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:robust to various modifications to our empirical design and that conditioning on industry IPO 
25:611:53256:27:38:72:397:478:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:waves is crucial to identify similar firms in an initial growth stage.  
25:612:53328:38:37:72:231:440:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:III.C.  Panel regression analysis 
25:613:53361:37:28:90:542:403:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In  Table VI,  we  confirm  our  event-time  and  calendar-time  portfolio  results  using  panel 
25:614:53459:28:28:72:543:375:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:regressions which allow us to simultaneously control for other  firm / IPO characteristics that 
25:615:53555:28:38:72:330:347:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:could potentially explain the abnormal performance.  
25:616:53608:38:39:538:541:309:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:                                                                           
25:617:53675:39:42:491:494:270:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:                                                                    
25:618:53734:42:39:231:431:228:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:                       ∑                 .            (1) 
25:619:53786:39:27:72:535:189:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In regressions, we include the industry IPO wave fixed effects, and calculate the standard errors 
25:620:53884:27:28:72:513:162:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:from two-way clustering on both industry and year (Petersen, 2009).23 Our key variables of 
25:621:53975:28:37:72:534:134:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:interest are the two interaction terms of GMHigh with BMLow and  BMHigh. BMLow (BMHigh) is the 
25:622:54070:37:7:216:219:97:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:                                                 
25:623:54118:7:16:72:544:90:6:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:23 Alternative ways to control fixed effects, such as industry fixed effects only or both industry and year fixed effects, 
25:624:54241:16:0:72:223:74:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:produce qualitatively similar results.  
26:625:54284:0:28:72:531:709:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:dummy variable for low (high) initial BM group, based on sorting all IPO stocks in an industry 
26:626:54379:28:28:72:533:681:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:IPO wave on BM at the end of event year 3. Consistent with our portfolio analysis, we measure 
26:627:54473:28:27:72:532:653:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:GM as the average gross margin in the first two fiscal years after the industry IPO wave ending 
26:628:54569:27:28:72:539:626:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:year. GMHigh is the dummy variable for high initial GM group, based on sorting all IPO stocks in 
26:629:54666:28:27:72:528:598:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:an industry IPO wave on GM within each BM group at the end of event year 3. Our dependent 
26:630:54756:27:28:72:534:571:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:variables are annual industry-adjusted stock returns in percentage points during event years 4 to 
26:631:54854:28:38:72:87:543:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:7.  
26:632:54857:38:27:90:543:505:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In the first regression (Model 1), we control for annual stock characteristics such as size, BM, 
26:633:54954:27:28:72:543:478:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:past return, and turnover that have been shown to have predictive power about future returns in 
26:634:55050:28:27:72:543:450:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the literature. Size is measured as the log market capitalization at the end of the previous year, 
26:635:55149:27:28:72:543:423:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and BM is the ratio of book equity to market capitalization at the end of the previous year, where 
26:636:55248:28:28:72:543:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:book equity precedes the year end by at least 3 months. Turnover is the sum of monthly share 
26:637:55341:28:27:72:543:367:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:turnover in the previous year. We find a positive and significant coefficient on BMLow* GMHigh 
26:638:55435:27:28:72:547:340:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:(7.62  with a t-value of 2.03), suggesting that among growth IPO stocks, those with a low gross 
26:639:55531:28:27:72:543:312:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:margin in the initial years after IPO subsequently underperform their high gross margin peers by 
26:640:55628:27:28:72:543:285:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:7.62% per annum in the period event years 4 to 7, consistent with our hypothesis. Interestingly, 
26:641:55725:28:28:72:542:257:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:GM has no predictive power among IPO firms with relatively high book-to-market equity ratios 
26:642:55818:28:27:72:542:229:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:in the initial years after IPOs, consistent with earlier results in both event-time and calendar-time 
26:643:55920:27:38:72:163:202:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:portfolio analyses. 
26:644:55940:38:27:90:543:164:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In the second regression (Model 2), we further control for a list of IPO characteristics that 
26:645:56034:27:28:72:543:137:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:may predict long-run IPO performance, including the IPO first-day return, a dummy variable that 
26:646:56130:28:28:72:539:109:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:equals 1 if the IPO has venture capital backing, a dummy variable that equals 1 if there is a lock-
26:647:56229:28:0:72:543:81:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:up condition, and the percent of primary (new) shares sold in the IPO. Consistent with Brav and 
27:648:56328:0:28:72:543:709:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Gompers (2003), IPOs with lockup restrictions are associated with significantly lower long-run 
27:649:56423:28:28:72:543:681:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:excess returns. There is very weak evidence that IPOs backed by venture capital are associated 
27:650:56518:28:27:72:543:653:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:with  better  long-run  performance,  which  is  also  consistent  with  Brav  and  Gompers  (1997) 
27:651:56618:27:28:72:543:626:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:although  the  coefficient  is  not  statistically  significant.  After  controlling  for  these  IPO 
27:652:56720:28:27:72:543:598:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:characteristics, the coefficient on BMLow*GMHigh is almost unchanged and still significant. To 
27:653:56815:27:28:72:543:571:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:conclude, the panel regressions confirm that the underperformance of the low-BM-low-GM IPO 
27:654:56906:28:38:72:338:543:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:firms is significant both economically and statistically. 
27:655:56964:38:27:90:543:505:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In  the  third  regression  (Model  3),  we  interact  the  BM  dummies  with  a  dummy  variable 
27:656:57062:27:28:72:543:478:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:indicating  high  asset  turnover  (AT)  instead  of  GM.  Interestingly,  while  higher  AT  predicts 
27:657:57165:28:27:72:543:450:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:higher future performance, this predictive power is stronger among high-BM IPOs, although the 
27:658:57259:27:38:72:435:423:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:regression coefficient on neither interaction term is statistically significant. 
27:659:57340:38:27:90:543:385:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Finally, in the fourth regression (Model 4), we interact the BM dummies with both high GM 
27:660:57430:27:28:72:543:358:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and high AT dummy variables. The regression highlights the differential roles played by GM and 
27:661:57525:28:28:72:543:330:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:AT. AT is  a significant  predictor of future performance among high-BM  IPOs.  This  relation 
27:662:57620:28:27:72:543:302:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:could be mechanical. To the extent that high-BM firms are associated with less growth options, 
27:663:57715:27:28:72:542:275:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the utilization rate of their current assets, as measured by AT, is a good indicator of their future 
27:664:57816:28:28:72:543:247:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:cash flows. Holding valuation ratio (BM) constant, firms with higher ATs (thus higher future 
27:665:57909:28:37:72:398:219:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:cash flows) should then be associated with higher expected returns. 
27:666:57977:37:28:90:542:182:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In contrast, lower GM is a stronger indicator of poor future performance among low-BM 
27:667:58063:28:27:72:543:154:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:IPOs. This result is unlikely to be mechanical. Untabulated results suggest that low-BM-low-GM 
27:668:58158:27:28:72:542:127:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:stocks have future average raw returns close to or even below the risk-free rates. Such a low 
27:669:58252:28:0:72:543:99:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:average return is difficult to reconcile with a positive risk premium for bearing economy-wide 
28:670:58350:0:28:72:543:709:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:systematic risk. Instead, a low GM could be associated with a risky pricing strategy for gaining 
28:671:58447:28:28:72:543:681:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:market share in the initial growth stage of a firm’s life cycle. Our findings thus suggest that the 
28:672:58547:28:37:72:445:653:12:g_d0_f2:12:Times New Roman:prices of such firms may reflect the unfulfilled optimistic views of investors.  
28:673:58627:37:38:247:367:616:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:IV. Additional analysis 
28:674:58650:38:27:90:543:578:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:So  far  we  have  provided  strong  evidence  supporting  the  prediction  of  Aghion  and  Stein 
28:675:58749:27:28:72:543:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:(2008) that low-GM firms in a growth equilibrium were initially overpriced and underperform in 
28:676:58844:28:28:72:543:523:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the long run. In this section, we investigate a comprehensive list of characteristics on these firms 
28:677:58945:28:27:72:543:495:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and  their  high-GM  counterparts  over  time  since  IPO,  aiming  to  shed  further  light  on  the 
28:678:59047:27:28:72:543:468:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:underlying economic mechanism that generated the initial overpricing. These analyses also help 
28:679:59142:28:37:72:352:440:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:to rule out several alternative explanations for our results. 
28:680:59204:37:38:72:255:403:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:IV.A. Price sensitivity to sales growth 
28:681:59244:38:28:90:543:365:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A key ingredient to the growth equilibrium in Aghion and Stein (2008) is a market pricing 
28:682:59334:28:27:72:542:337:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:rule that over-fixates on sales growth numbers. We provide direct supporting evidence for such a 
28:683:59431:27:28:72:543:310:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:pricing rule by examining the market price response to surprises in earnings and sales growth. 
28:684:59526:28:38:72:491:282:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Specifically, we run the following regressions following Anthony and Ramesh (1992): 
28:685:59610:38:39:383:539:244:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f2:                                               ,                       (2) 
28:686:59681:39:28:72:543:205:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:where ExRetq is the quarterly industry-adjusted return over the 3-month period from the end of 
28:687:59776:28:27:72:543:177:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the first calendar month of quarter q to the end of the first calendar month of quarter q+1. ΔSGq 
28:688:59873:27:28:72:543:150:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:is the change in sales growth rate from calendar quarter q-1 to q, where the sales growth rate in 
28:689:59971:28:27:72:543:122:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:quarter  q  is  calculated  as  (Salesq  -  Salesq-4)/  Salesq-4.  ΔIBq  is  the  year-over-year  change  in 
28:690:60080:27:0:72:543:95:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:quarterly  earnings,  calculated  as  (IBq  -   IBq-4)/  MVq-4,  where  IBq  is  the  income  before 
29:691:60184:0:28:72:543:709:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:extraordinary items in quarter q and MVq is the market capitalization at the end of quarter q. 
29:692:60279:28:28:72:543:681:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:ΔCAPXq is the year-over-year change in quarterly capital expenditure, calculated as (CAPXq - 
29:693:60372:28:27:72:543:653:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:CAPXq-4)/  MVq-4,  where  CAPXq  is  the  capital  expenditure  in  quarter  q.  The  regression 
29:694:60469:27:28:72:543:626:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:specification is for evaluating whether stock prices are responding to sales growth news after 
29:695:60564:28:27:72:543:598:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:controlling for earnings news and investment news. We run the regressions separately for each 
29:696:60658:27:28:72:542:571:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:BM/GM portfolio in each year during the 7 years after event year 0. Our hypothesis is that the 
29:697:60753:28:28:72:542:543:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:slope coefficient    should be positive and larger for low-BM-low-GM stocks when compared to 
29:698:60843:28:28:72:542:515:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:low-   BM-h igh-GM stocks in the initial years after IPO as the investors who follow those stocks 
29:699:60941:28:37:72:297:487:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:are more likely to over-fixate on sales growth. 
29:700:60989:37:28:90:543:450:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In Table VII, we report these sales growth response coefficients, which are the regression 
29:701:61080:28:28:72:542:422:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:coefficients on ΔSGq, and associated t-statistics. We also report the difference in the coefficients 
29:702:61181:28:27:72:543:394:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:between high and low GM groups and the associated t-statistics. All t-statistics are calculated 
29:703:61277:27:28:72:543:367:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:based on the standard errors clustered by industry. To obtain the industry benchmark of the sales 
29:704:61375:28:27:72:543:339:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:response coefficient, we run similar regressions for a sample of all stocks in the industry which 
29:705:61473:27:38:72:479:312:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:were listed at least 3 years before the ending year of the current industry IPO wave.  
29:706:61560:38:27:90:543:274:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Consistent with the market’s over-fixation on sales, stock prices react significantly to sales 
29:707:61655:27:28:72:542:247:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:growth rates among all industry IPO wave stocks during the first two years after the wave ending 
29:708:61752:28:28:72:540:219:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:year, even after controlling for contemporaneous earnings surprises. This is more so for the low-
29:709:61849:28:27:72:543:191:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:GM stocks. In the first year after the industry IPO wave, a 1% increase in quarterly sales growth 
29:710:61947:27:28:72:543:164:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:rate translates to 8 basis points in the quarterly stock return. Interestingly, after event year 3, the 
29:711:62051:28:28:72:543:136:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:low-GM stocks no longer have significant sales growth response coefficients, which is consistent 
29:712:62148:28:27:72:543:108:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:with the notion that the market starts to notice the overpricing among the low-GM stocks and the 
29:713:62245:27:0:72:258:81:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:market price adjusts itself downward.  
30:714:62287:0:38:72:332:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:IV.B. Factors driving the long-run underperformance 
30:715:62339:38:27:90:543:671:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Aghion and Stein (2008) models investor bounded rationality by assuming that they follow a 
30:716:62430:27:28:72:543:644:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:simple linear rule in forecasting future valuation relevant variables. Observing the initial high 
30:717:62528:28:28:72:543:616:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:sales growth rates on the low-GM firms, investors might over-estimate the firm’s earnings power 
30:718:62624:28:27:72:543:588:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:in the future. This optimism is likely amplified by the two-way feedback mechanism between 
30:719:62715:27:28:72:543:561:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:firms’  strategies  and  the  market’s  pricing  rule,  causing  large  initial  overpricing.  Over  time, 
30:720:62822:28:28:72:542:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:correction in these errors-in-expectation leads to long-run underperformance. In this subsection, 
30:721:62920:28:27:72:543:505:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:we provide direct evidence for the initial investor optimism and detailed analysis of the price 
30:722:63016:27:38:72:166:478:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:correction process. 
30:723:63036:38:27:90:543:440:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Table VIII shows additional portfolio-level characteristics over years after the industry IPO 
30:724:63130:27:28:72:543:413:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:wave ending  year for the high-GM and low-GM growth portfolios, their differences, and the 
30:725:63221:28:27:72:543:385:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:same  characteristics  for  the  industry  benchmark.  Panel  A  reports  the  post-formation  annual 
30:726:63323:27:28:72:540:358:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:frequencies for performance-related delisting. Consistent with the return results, low-BM-low-
30:727:63417:28:28:72:543:330:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:GM IPO firms experience significantly more delisting than their high-GM counterparts. More 
30:728:63508:28:27:72:540:302:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:than 18% of them were delisted by the end of event year 7 whereas less than 9% of the low-BM-
30:729:63601:27:28:72:543:275:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:high-GM  firms  were  delisted  during  the  same  period,  confirming  that  growing  sales  at  the 
30:730:63703:28:38:72:360:247:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:expense of profitability is indeed not a sustainable strategy. 
30:731:63766:38:27:90:542:209:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Firms may deliberately keep prices and GM low in the early stages of their life cycle with the 
30:732:63861:27:28:72:543:182:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:expectation  that  it  will  help  them  gain  market  share  and  greater  future  profits  via  increased 
30:733:63969:28:27:72:543:154:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:pricing power and/or permanent cost advantages arising from economies of scale. Our findings 
30:734:64062:27:28:72:549:127:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:suggest that such expectations, if they were there to start with, were not fulfilled in our sample.   
30:735:64164:28:0:72:542:99:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In Panel B, when we examine the market share of low-BM-low-GM IPO firms, it only grows 
31:736:64254:0:28:72:542:709:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:from 0.12 to 0.17 from event year 3 to 7. In contrast, the low-BM-high-GM IPO firms actually 
31:737:64347:28:28:72:542:681:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:grow their market share faster in the same period from 0.14 to 0.23. The lower market share, 
31:738:64440:28:27:72:540:653:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:coupled with a low GM, not surprisingly leads to a subpar operating performance of low-BM-
31:739:64530:27:28:72:543:626:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:low-GM IPO firms. Return on assets (ROA) of low-BM-low-GM firms is significantly worse 
31:740:64617:28:27:72:543:598:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:than  their  high-GM  peers  throughout  the  seven  event  years  after  the  IPO  wave  ending  year. 
31:741:64721:27:28:72:547:571:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Overall, evidence in Panels A and B suggests that low-BM-low -GM firms have deteriorating 
31:742:64811:28:28:72:542:543:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:operating performance in the long-run relative to low-BM-    high-GM firms, and investors who use 
31:743:64909:28:37:72:502:515:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:simple linear extrapolation in forecasting, are likely to be too optimistic at the beginning. 
31:744:65003:37:28:90:543:478:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Stock returns are driven by revisions in future cash flow expectations rather the cash flow 
31:745:65095:28:27:72:543:450:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:realizations  themselves.  In  what  follows,  we  use  analyst  forecasts  to  examine  cash  flow 
31:746:65195:27:28:72:543:423:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:expectations for various horizons at the portfolio formation date (the end of event year 3) and 
31:747:65291:28:28:72:543:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:trace the revisions in these forecasts over time from event year 3 to event year 7. This analysis 
31:748:65389:28:27:72:542:367:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:provides additional  insights  on  the  exact  source  of  error-in-expectation  that  drives  the  initial 
31:749:65497:27:38:72:133:340:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:overpricing. 
31:750:65510:38:27:90:543:302:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Specifically, we proceed in the following steps to estimate the expectations of future cash 
31:751:65602:27:38:72:232:275:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:flows at the end of event year 3.  
31:752:65637:38:28:90:542:237:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In the first step, we forecast future earnings of the value-weighted portfolio of all stocks in a 
31:753:65735:28:27:72:543:209:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:BM/GM portfolio in an industry IPO wave based on IBES forecasts of earnings and earnings 
31:754:65824:27:28:72:543:182:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:growth rate. The forecasted earnings for the first two years (event years 4 and 5) are taken from 
31:755:65922:28:27:72:543:154:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:IBES consensus (mean) earnings forecasts. Earnings are then assumed to grow in the next three 
31:756:66016:27:28:72:543:127:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:years (event years 6 to 8) at the IBES consensus (mean) long-term growth rate forecasts (LTG). 
31:757:66111:28:0:72:543:99:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:We take the value-weighted average of LTGs of all stocks in a portfolio to form the portfolio's 
32:758:66210:0:28:72:547:709:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:LTG. Finally, earnings growth rate is assumed to converge linearly to a steady growth rate (SGR) 
32:759:66307:28:28:72:543:681:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:in the next 10 years (event years 9 to 18). We use the median value of all long-term earnings 
32:760:66401:28:37:72:345:653:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:growth rate forecasts in IBES as the steady growth rate.  
32:761:66459:37:28:90:543:616:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In the second step, we forecast the book equity values in future years. We first assume a 
32:762:66549:28:27:72:543:588:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:constant dividend payout ratio (DPR) relative to the cum-dividend book equity value, i.e., Dt = 
32:763:66645:27:28:72:542:561:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:(BEt- 1 + Et)*DPR, where Dt is the estimated dividend in year t, BEt- 1 is the estimated book equity 
32:764:66746:28:28:72:542:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:value in year t-1, and Et is the estimated earnings in year t. For simplicity, we assume a 5% value 
32:765:66846:28:27:72:543:505:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:for DPR based on the historical average values of all firms in COMPUSTAT. We then calculate 
32:766:66938:27:38:72:536:478:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the forecasted book equity values assuming the clean surplus relation, i.e., BEt = BEt- 1 + Et -  Dt.  
32:767:67041:38:27:90:543:440:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In the third step, we calculate the forecasted ROEs for all future years. Based on forecasted 
32:768:67135:27:28:72:543:413:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:earnings  and  book  equity  values  in  the  next  15  years  (event  years  4  to  18),  we  calculate 
32:769:67240:28:27:72:543:385:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:forecasted ROEs in these years, FROEt = Et / BEt-1. Forecasted ROE for all years in the steady 
32:770:67335:27:28:72:543:358:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:state (SROE), i.e., those years after event year 18, is calculated as (1+SGR)/(1-DPR) - 1, based 
32:771:67432:28:38:72:474:330:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:on the equilibrium relationship among these parameters in the steady growth state.  
32:772:67516:38:29:90:543:292:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:In the final step, following Da and Warachka (2009), we form the future cash flow estimate 
32:773:67607:29:29:72:543:263:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:as  the  discounted  sum  of  all  future  log  ROEs,       ∑                   .  Following 
32:774:67696:29:29:72:543:234:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Vuolteenaho (2002) and Campbell and Vuolneenaho (2004), we assume a constant value, 0.95, 
32:775:67786:29:28:72:542:205:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:for , which is estimated from the historical values of market and book dividend yields of all 
32:776:67881:28:38:72:232:177:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:stocks in CRSP/COMPUSTAT.  
32:777:67908:38:27:90:542:139:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:At the end of event  year 7, we update the cash flow estimate (ESUM) for each BM/GM 
32:778:67992:27:0:72:543:112:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:group in each industry IPO wave. Forecasted ROEs in event years 4 to 7 are replaced with the 
33:779:68088:0:28:72:543:709:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:realized values. For all other years after event year 7, the forecasted ROEs are updated, following 
33:780:68188:28:37:72:311:681:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the same forecasting procedure described above.  
33:781:68237:37:28:90:543:644:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:We then compute the change in cash flow estimate (∆ESUM) from event year 3 to event year 
33:782:68326:28:28:72:543:616:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:7 for each BM/GM group in each industry IPO wave. Finally, we use the number of IPOs at the 
33:783:68418:28:27:72:543:588:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:end of event  year 3 in a wave to  weight across all  industry  IPO waves to estimate the final 
33:784:68514:27:29:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f2:statistics of each BM/GM group. We also break down ∆ESUM into three components: ∆ESUM4-
33:785:68601:29:27:72:543:532:8:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:7 which is due to errors in short-run forecasted ROEs of event years 4 to 7, ∆ESUM8- 12 which is 
33:786:68698:27:27:72:543:505:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:due to revision in medium-run forecasted ROEs of event years 8 to 12, and ∆ESUM13-inf which is 
33:787:68793:27:38:72:445:478:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:due to revision in long-run forecasted ROEs from event year 13 and beyond.  
33:788:68868:38:27:90:543:440:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The results are reported in Panel C of Table VIII. For each BM/GM portfolio, we report the 
33:789:68959:27:28:72:543:413:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:weighted mean and the t-statistics for ∆ESUMs. We also report the difference in the mean and 
33:790:69052:28:27:72:543:385:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the associated statistics  between high and low  GM groups  for ∆ESUMs.  We also  obtain the 
33:791:69145:27:28:72:543:358:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:industry benchmarks of ∆ESUMs in the following steps. First, for each industry IPO wave, we 
33:792:69237:28:28:72:543:330:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:select all stocks in the same industry as those in the wave which were listed at least 3 years 
33:793:69332:28:27:72:543:302:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:before event year 0 to form the value-weighted control portfolio. Second, we estimate ∆ESUMs 
33:794:69425:27:28:72:543:275:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:for  each  wave  control  portfolio,  following  the  same  procedure  for  the  industry  IPO  wave 
33:795:69526:28:27:72:543:247:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:portfolios. Finally, we use the number of IPOs at the end of event year 3 in the corresponding 
33:796:69621:27:28:72:543:220:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:industry IPO wave to weight across all wave control portfolios to estimate the final statistics of 
33:797:69720:28:38:72:191:192:12:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the industry benchmark. 
33:798:69744:38:27:90:543:154:11:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2: When we compare the low-GM firms to the high-GM firms in Panel C, we find that although 
33:799:69832:27:28:72:543:127:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:both groups experience downward revisions in cash flow expectations from event year 3 to event 
33:800:69927:28:0:72:543:99:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:year 7, the downward revisions are larger (in absolute term) for low-GM firms. In other words, 
34:801:70025:0:28:72:543:709:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:low-GM  firms  experience  more  negative  cash  flow  news,  which  explains  their  relative 
34:802:70120:28:28:72:543:681:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:underperformance. Most interestingly, when we look at different cash flow forecast horizons, we 
34:803:70216:28:27:72:543:653:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:find that the revisions in cash flow forecasts for the very long-run horizon (event year 13 and 
34:804:70312:27:28:72:543:626:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:onwards) are significantly more negative for the low-GM firms. This result suggests that the 
34:805:70405:28:27:72:543:598:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:relative initial overpricing of low-GM firms is likely a result of optimism associated with the 
34:806:70501:27:28:72:543:571:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:firm earnings power in the very long run. This result also partly explains why the overpricing 
34:807:70596:28:38:72:298:543:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:takes so long (almost 4 years) to be corrected.  
34:808:70645:38:37:72:209:505:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:IV.C. Uncertainty measures 
34:809:70672:37:28:72:543:468:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:   We  have  argued  that  industry  IPO  waves  are  a  great  setting  for  studying  the  growth 
34:810:70772:28:27:72:543:440:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:equilibrium in Aghion and Stein (2008). IPO firms have short tracking records to offer but are 
34:811:70867:27:28:72:543:413:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:associated with high potential growth rates at the same time. Due to the resulting uncertainty 
34:812:70962:28:27:72:543:385:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:associated  with  their  future  earning  power,  investors  are  more  likely  to  over-fixate  on  sales 
34:813:71069:27:28:72:543:358:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:numbers in valuation at least initially, thus satisfying the key assumption in Aghion and Stein 
34:814:71165:28:38:72:110:330:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:(2008). 
34:815:71173:38:27:90:543:292:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:To test this key assumption we first examine the cash flow uncertainty associated with IPO 
34:816:71264:27:28:72:543:265:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:firms using textual analysis of the Risk Factors sections of the IPO prospectus. According to 
34:817:71358:28:28:72:543:237:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Hanley and Hoberg (2010), “the Risk Factors section ... is the only section that has significant 
34:818:71455:28:27:72:543:209:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:loadings on both positive and negative tone. This is consistent with its role in describing the 
34:819:71551:27:28:72:543:182:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f2:second  moment  of  the  outcomes  (high  and  low), as its namesake suggests it should (pg 2857, 
34:820:71649:28:27:72:543:154:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:italics added).” Thus, more frequent occurrence of words related to “cost(s)” or “profitability” 
34:821:71746:27:28:72:542:127:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:may signal higher expected cash flow uncertainty in the future. Loughran and McDonald (2011) 
34:822:71839:28:0:72:542:99:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:carefully  construct  word  lists  that  are  particularly  powerful  in  financial  applications  and 
35:823:71945:0:28:72:543:709:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Loughran and McDonald (2013) update their lists for the IPO sample and show them to be useful 
35:824:72039:28:28:72:543:681:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:in explaining IPO first-day return and subsequent volatilities. As we are focusing on measuring 
35:825:72135:28:27:72:543:653:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:cash flow uncertainty within a specific section of IPO prospectuses, we do not use the more 
35:826:72227:27:38:72:377:626:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:general-purpose word lists in Loughran and McDonald (2013). 
35:827:72287:38:27:90:543:588:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:We  obtain  IPO  prospectuses  from  SEC  Edgar  for  stocks  in  industry  IPO  waves  with  an 
35:828:72384:27:28:72:543:561:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:offering date after 1994. For each IPO, we keep only the most recent filing during the window 
35:829:72478:28:28:72:543:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:from 1095 days before the IPO filing date to 30 days after the IPO filing date. Panel A of Table 
35:830:72575:28:27:72:543:505:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:IX reports preliminary results from the IPO prospectus for the four portfolios of industry IPO 
35:831:72670:27:28:72:543:478:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:wave stocks. More than half of our sample stocks have valid IPO prospectus and associated Risk 
35:832:72765:28:37:72:507:450:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Factor sections. The coverage is similar across the four portfolios sorted on BM and GM.  
35:833:72855:37:28:90:564:413:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Overall, low-BM-low-   GM IPOs are indeed associated with more mentions of “Cost(s)” and 
35:834:72944:28:27:72:543:385:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:“Profitability” in their Risk Factors sections.  While this is consistent with expected cash flow 
35:835:73042:27:28:72:543:358:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:uncertainty  being  higher  among  these  IPOs,  we  need  to  keep  in  mind  the  limited  precision 
35:836:73145:28:28:72:543:330:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:associated with these findings due to the fact that we were able to examine the prospectuses for 
35:837:73242:28:27:72:543:302:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:only  a  small  subset  of  the  IPOs.  Higher  cash  flow  uncertainty  could  lead  to  higher  return 
35:838:73347:27:28:72:542:275:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:idiosyncratic volatility in the face of intense product market competition (see Irvine and Pontiff 
35:839:73446:28:28:72:543:247:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:(2009)), thus making it less attractive to risk-averse arbitrageurs to  arbitrage away the initial 
35:840:73545:28:37:72:144:219:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:overvaluation. 
35:841:73560:37:28:72:543:182:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:   We further examine two additional measures of uncertainty using the analyst forecasts and 
35:842:73653:28:27:72:543:154:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:stock prices after the IPO. Diether, Malloy and Scherbina (2002) find that stocks with higher 
35:843:73747:27:28:72:543:127:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:analyst forecast dispersion are likely to underperform in the future, compared with their peers 
35:844:73843:28:0:72:543:99:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:with  lower  forecast  dispersion.  They  interpret  their  results  as  consistent  with  the  argument 
36:845:73951:0:28:72:543:709:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:proposed  in  Miller  (1977)  that  higher  difference-of-opinion,  combined  with  short-sales 
36:846:74047:28:28:72:543:681:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:constraints, could lead to temporary overvaluation. In light of the recent finding in Cheong and 
36:847:74144:28:27:72:543:653:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Thomas  (2011)  that  analyst  forecast  dispersion  does  not  vary  with  scale,  we  measure  the 
36:848:74245:27:28:72:543:626:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:dispersion as the standard deviation of analyst forecasts of current fiscal year's earnings per share 
36:849:74347:28:27:72:542:598:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:as reported by IBES. In Panel B of Table IX, we report the statistics on the measure of analyst 
36:850:74443:27:28:72:546:571:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:earnings  forecast  dispersion.  Low-BM-low -GM  IPO  firms  are  consistently  associated  with 
36:851:74540:28:28:72:543:543:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:greater dispersion  in  their earnings  forecasts, especially during the  early  years after the  IPO, 
36:852:74643:28:27:72:543:515:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:which is consistent with the notion that the significant degree of uncertainty concerning these 
36:853:74739:27:28:72:543:488:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:growth firms could acerbate the initial overvaluation for firms pursuing unsustainable business 
36:854:74835:28:37:72:123:460:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:strategies. 
36:855:74847:37:28:90:543:423:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:We  also  report  the  idiosyncratic  volatility  of  firms  in  Panel  B.  To  estimate  a  firm's 
36:856:74947:28:28:72:543:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:idiosyncratic  volatility  in  year  t,  following  Ang,  Hodrick,  Xing  and  Zhang  (2006),  we  first 
36:857:75052:28:27:72:543:367:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:regress its daily stock returns in year t on Fama-French three factors (MKTRF, SMB and HML) 
36:858:75144:27:28:72:543:340:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and  Carhart's  momentum  factor  (UMD),  and  then  calculate  the  standard  deviation  of  the 
36:859:75242:28:27:72:543:312:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:residuals. To mitigate the skewness in the distribution, we take the natural log of the estimated 
36:860:75340:27:28:72:543:285:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:idiosyncratic  volatility.  Overall,  low-GM  growth  firms  are  associated  with  much  higher 
36:861:75437:28:28:72:543:257:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:idiosyncratic volatilities and these volatilities gradually decline over time after the IPO. Pastor 
36:862:75537:28:27:72:543:229:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and Veronesi (2003) argue that the uncertainty associated with the IPO firms could result in high 
36:863:75635:27:28:72:543:202:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:initial  valuation  and  the  subsequent  learning  about  profitability  reduces  the  uncertainty  and 
36:864:75740:28:27:72:543:174:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:valuation,  explaining  the  IPO  long-run  underperformance.  While  such  a  learning  mechanism 
36:865:75839:27:28:72:543:147:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:could be consistent with the long-run underperformance of IPOs as a group, it should not drive 
36:866:75934:28:0:72:543:119:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the relative underperformance of low-BM-low-GM IPOs within an industry IPO wave as we do 
37:867:76026:0:28:72:543:709:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:not observe a greater reduction in idiosyncratic volatility over time for the low-GM growth firms 
37:868:76124:28:38:72:269:681:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:relative to their high-GM counterparts.24 
37:869:76165:38:37:72:277:643:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:IV.D. Investor type and limits to arbitrage 
37:870:76209:37:28:90:546:606:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2: We  obtain  further  insights  about  the  overpricing  of  low-BM-low -GM  IPO  stocks  by 
37:871:76302:28:27:72:543:578:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:examining the holdings by corporate insiders and mutual funds over years after IPO. Table X 
37:872:76394:27:28:72:543:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:reveals  some  interesting  patterns  about  the  holdings  of  these  potentially  better  informed  / 
37:873:76498:28:28:72:547:523:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:sophisticated investors on the two groups of growth IPO stocks. On average, low-BM-low -GM 
37:874:76589:28:27:72:543:495:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:IPO  stocks  are  held  significantly  less  by  insiders  and  mutual  funds  (including  those  with  a 
37:875:76695:27:28:72:540:468:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:growth-style) when compared to their high-GM peers, especially during earlier years.25 The low-
37:876:76790:28:27:72:543:440:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:BM-low-GM growth IPO firms seem to have developed a clientele for relatively  more naïve 
37:877:76879:27:38:72:435:413:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:investors who are more likely to suffer from over-reliance on sales growth. 
37:878:76955:38:28:90:543:375:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Overall,  greater  uncertainties  and  lower  ownership  by  sophisticated  /  potentially  better 
37:879:77054:28:27:72:542:347:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:informed investors, in the presence of limits-to-arbitrage such as direct or indirect short-selling 
37:880:77154:27:28:72:543:320:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:constraints and high idiosyncratic risk, may explain why it takes three to four years for the initial 
37:881:77256:28:27:72:543:292:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:over-valuation to disappear. Our findings are consistent with Stambaugh, Yu and Yuan (2012) 
37:882:77348:27:28:72:543:265:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:who find that asset pricing anomalies are generally stronger following high levels of investor 
37:883:77443:28:28:72:542:237:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:sentiment, and in long-short strategies that exploit anomalies, the short leg of the strategies is 
37:884:77542:28:38:72:318:209:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:more profitable following high investor sentiment. 
37:885:77593:38:16:216:219:171:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:  
37:886:77593:16:8:216:219:155:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:                                                 
37:887:77641:8:16:72:538:147:6:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:24 The untabulated test shows that the reduction in log idiosyncratic volatility from event year 3 to event year 7 does 
37:888:77761:16:7:72:279:131:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:not differ significantly across two groups of firms.  
37:889:77815:7:16:72:509:124:6:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:25 We obtain the holdings of corporate insiders via Thomson Reuters Insiders Filing database and include the 
37:890:77924:16:11:72:537:108:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:holdings of insiders with relationship to firms up to level 3 (senior executives). We obtain the mutual fund holdings 
37:891:78042:11:12:72:503:97:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:via Thomson Reuters Mutual Fund Holdings database (S12), and classify mutual funds into different styles 
37:892:78147:12:11:72:522:85:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:according to their investment objective codes in S12, supplemented by the style information from CRSP mutual 
37:893:78256:11:0:72:434:74:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:fund data. Funds with a growth or aggressive growth style are classified as growth funds.  
38:894:78350:0:41:268:346:708:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:V. Conclusion 
38:895:78363:41:28:90:543:667:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The predictability of stock returns based on valuation ratios, like E/P, P/B, and C/P etc., is 
38:896:78458:28:27:72:543:639:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:well documented in the literature.  In a recent paper, Novy-Marx (2012) shows that firms with 
38:897:78552:27:28:72:542:612:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:high gross-profit-to-asset ratio (GPA) earn higher returns going forward, even after controlling 
38:898:78649:28:27:72:542:584:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:for their book-to-market equity ratios. However the debate as to whether such predictability is 
38:899:78745:27:28:72:543:557:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:evidence  against  market  efficiency  in  economically  important  ways  has  been  the  subject  of 
38:900:78847:28:28:72:543:529:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:continuing debate. Investors may well be aware of such predictability and still agree with the 
38:901:78942:28:27:72:543:501:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:market that the prices are right; the higher than average predicted returns on some stocks may be 
38:902:79040:27:28:72:543:474:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:compensation for risks that investors care about and may be difficult to identify using historical 
38:903:79139:28:41:72:101:446:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:data.  
38:904:79146:41:28:90:543:405:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:The papers in the more recent literature support the view that some (could be a small part) of 
38:905:79241:28:28:72:543:377:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the predictability may reflect psychological biases built into the way investors make decisions, 
38:906:79338:28:27:72:543:349:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:and agency issues limit the ability of more sophisticated arbitrageurs who have to rely on other 
38:907:79435:27:28:72:543:322:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:people’s  money  from  exploiting  any  profit  opportunities  that  may  arise  from  such 
38:908:79527:28:27:72:543:294:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:predictability.  Our findings contribute to this literature by identifying situations when prices of 
38:909:79628:27:28:72:542:267:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:some stocks are likely to be affected by bounded rationality or biases in the way investors make 
38:910:79725:28:42:72:123:239:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:decisions. 
38:911:79736:42:27:90:543:197:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Our findings support the hypothesis in Aghion and Stein (2008) that there are time periods 
38:912:79827:27:28:72:543:170:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:when market conditions are more favorable to growth firms, and during those times firms with 
38:913:79920:28:27:72:543:142:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:strong growth but weak margins will be overvalued. Taking advantage of industry IPO waves as 
38:914:80013:27:28:72:543:115:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:a natural setting for studying a homogenous group of firms in the same growth stage of their life 
38:915:80111:28:0:72:543:87:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:cycles,  we  find  that  among  firms  that  went  public  during  an  industry  IPO  wave,  those  with 
39:916:80219:0:28:72:543:709:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:relatively high valuations and historical sales growth rates, but low gross margins during the first 
39:917:80320:28:28:72:543:681:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:three years after the wave under-perform their industry peers by more than 1% per month during 
39:918:80415:28:27:72:543:653:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:the subsequent four-year period, after adjusting for risk differentials. Greater uncertainties and 
39:919:80514:27:28:72:543:626:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:lower ownership by sophisticated, better informed investors associated with these firms, in the 
39:920:80610:28:27:72:542:598:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:presence  of  limits-to-arbitrage  such  as  direct  or  indirect  short-selling  constraints  and  high 
39:921:80715:27:0:72:543:571:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:idiosyncratic risk, may explain why it takes so long for the initial over-valuation to disappear.

43:1057:90105:13:13:285:510:252:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Timeline of our portfolio formation procedure 
43:1058:90151:13:13:72:723:239:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We follow the procedure in Chemmanur and He (2011) to identify industry IPO waves based on how clustered the IPOs are in an industry. For 
43:1059:90289:13:13:72:722:226:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:each industry IPO wave, the calendar year in which the wave ended is denoted as event year 0. We form portfolios within the wave at the end of 
43:1060:90432:13:12:72:723:213:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:event year 3, based on the book-to-market equity ratio (market price at the end of event year 3 and book equity preceding the market price by at 
43:1061:90577:12:13:72:722:201:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:least 3 months) and the average of gross margins (GM) during fiscal years 1 and 2. We do not use the GM in fiscal year 3 since such accounting 
43:1062:90720:13:13:72:723:188:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:information is not yet available at the end of event year 3 for many firms when we form the portfolios. In addition, we require at least 8 firms in an 
43:1063:90871:13:12:72:722:175:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:industry IPO wave at the end of event year 3 to ensure that our portfolio-level result is not driven by a single firm. The portfolios are then held for 
43:1064:91022:12:14:72:270:163:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:four years from event year 4 to event year 7.

46:1189:93398:13:12:72:75:369:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2: 
46:1190:93398:12:13:72:723:357:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Note: This table presents the descriptive statistics of industry IPO waves. We define industry IPO waves by Fama-French 49 industries based on 
46:1191:93541:13:13:72:723:344:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:how clustered the IPOs are in an industry. For each industry i and month t, we count the number of IPOs in the 3-month window from t-1 to t+1. 
46:1192:93684:13:12:72:723:331:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We then define a hot IPO month as a month with the 3-month number of IPOs in the top quartile of all IPO months from 1970 to 2010 in the 
46:1193:93821:12:13:72:723:319:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:industry. Finally, we classify IPOs in those consecutive hot months as a wave. We define the beginning month and the ending month of a wave as 
46:1194:93964:13:13:72:723:306:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the first month and the last month with IPOs in that wave. To avoid the problem that standalone IPOs are erroneously classified as a wave, we 
46:1195:94106:13:12:72:723:293:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:require a minimum of 5  IPOs in total and 1 IPO every  month  on average in the wave period. Our empirical analyses involve forming four 
46:1196:94243:12:13:72:723:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:portfolios within each industry IPO wave three years after the wave ending year (event year 0), based on the book-to-market equity ratio at the end 
46:1197:94391:13:12:72:723:268:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of event year 3 and the average profitability in the first two fiscal years after event year 0. We require a minimum of 8 IPOs with non-missing 
46:1198:94535:12:13:72:723:256:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:sorting variables at the portfolio formation time for a meaningful sort. After imposing these filters, 1425 IPOs going public during 68 industry IPO 
46:1199:94684:13:13:72:300:243:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:waves in the period 1980 to 2006 enter our sample. 
46:1200:94735:13:12:90:725:230:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Panel A presents the distribution of IPOs on and off waves during our sample period. Columns 2-4 present the distribution for all IPOs in SDC, 
46:1201:94878:12:13:72:723:218:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:excluding those in the 49th Fama-French industry or those not classified into any industry. Columns 5-7 present the distribution for those IPOs 
46:1202:95022:13:13:72:722:205:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:appearing in COMPUSTAT within 3 years after the listing year. And the final column presents the number of IPOs in our sample. Panel B 
46:1203:95156:13:12:72:723:192:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:presents the distribution of 68 industry IPO waves in our sample across Fama   -French 49 industries, and the  summary statistics for some wave 
46:1204:95300:12:13:72:722:180:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:characteristics such as the duration of the wave, the number of all IPOs in the wave, and the number of IPOs in the wave entering our final sample.

47:1258:96417:13:12:90:525:360:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Note: This table presents the industry-adjusted buy-and-hold returns of event-time portfolios of 
47:1259:96514:12:13:90:525:348:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:stocks in industry IPO waves in 7 years after the wave ending year (denoted as event year 0). For 
47:1260:96612:13:13:90:524:335:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:each industry IPO wave, we conduct a two-by-two sequential sort for IPOs in the wave on the 
47:1261:96704:13:12:90:524:322:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:book-to-market equity ratio (BM) at the end of event year 3 and the average gross margin (GM) 
47:1262:96798:12:13:90:525:310:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in fiscal years 1 and 2. Four event-time BM-GM portfolios are formed across all industry IPO 
47:1263:96891:13:13:90:525:297:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:waves. We first calculate buy-and-hold returns for each IPO stock in both the portfolio formation 
47:1264:96989:13:12:90:525:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:period and the portfolio holding period, then calculate the value-weighted average returns within 
47:1265:97087:12:13:90:525:272:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a  wave,  and  finally  obtain  the  wave-size-weighted  average  returns  across  all  waves.  For 
47:1266:97187:13:12:90:524:259:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:consistency of comparison, we use the market capitalization of individual stocks and the number 
47:1267:97283:12:13:90:525:247:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of IPOs in a wave at the time of portfolio formation, the end of event year 3, as weights for 
47:1268:97377:13:13:90:525:234:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:individual  stocks  and  waves  respectively.  The  industry  adjusted  buy-and-hold  returns  are 
47:1269:97476:13:12:90:525:221:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:calculated  as  the  buy-and-hold  returns  in  excess  of  the  buy-and-hold  value-weighted  average 
47:1270:97579:12:13:90:525:209:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:industry  returns  over  the corresponding  horizon.  We  report the average  returns  (%)  and  their 
47:1271:97682:13:13:90:525:196:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:heteroskedasticity-and-correlation consistent t-statistics, calculated using the approach proposed 
47:1272:97781:13:12:90:525:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:by Jegadeesh and Karceski (2009), for four BM-GM portfolios and the difference between high

53:1509:106396:12:13:90:524:634:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:on equity (ROE), in fiscal years 1 and 2. The last sub-panel presents the result of a two-by-two 
53:1510:106493:13:13:90:524:621:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:sequential sort on the average sales growth rate and the average gross margin in fiscal years 1 and 
53:1511:106593:13:12:90:525:608:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:2. Similar to our baseline trading strategy, all these trading strategies form portfolios at the end of 
53:1512:106697:12:13:90:331:596:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:event year 3 and hold them during the next four years. 
53:1513:106752:13:13:108:524:583:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In  panel  B,  we  partition  the  industry  IPO  waves  into  two  groups  based  on  competition 
53:1514:106851:13:12:90:525:570:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:measures of their affiliated industries. For each selected industry competition variable, we take 
53:1515:106949:12:13:90:524:558:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the average value of the variable in the first two fiscal years after event year 0 as the proxy of 
53:1516:107048:13:13:90:525:545:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:industry competition. The High-group (Low-group) refers to industry IPO waves with the value 
53:1517:107141:13:12:90:525:532:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of the industry competition measure above (below) the median value of the measure across all 
53:1518:107234:12:13:90:525:520:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:waves  in  our  sample.  We  then  form  BM-GM  portfolios  separately  among  IPOs  in  these  two 
53:1519:107334:13:13:90:524:507:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:groups of industry IPO waves, following the method in our baseline trading strategy. Herfindahl 
53:1520:107430:13:12:90:524:494:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:index of sales is the sum of squared market shares across all firms in an industry. Advertisement 
53:1521:107528:12:13:90:520:482:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:intensity is measured as the industry total advertising expenses scaled by the industry total sales.  
53:1522:107630:13:12:108:525:469:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In Panel C, we form BM-GM portfolios among non-IPO-wave samples, following methods 
53:1523:107713:12:13:90:525:457:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:similar  to  that  in  the  baseline  trading  strategy  on  our  IPO  wave  sample.  The  first  sub-panel 
53:1524:107821:13:13:90:524:444:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:presents the results of forming portfolios among all IPOs in the same industry which were listed 
53:1525:107918:13:12:90:525:431:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in the same year. First, IPOs in an industry-year IPO cohort are assigned into four groups at the 
53:1526:108016:12:13:90:525:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:end of the third year after the offering year based on a two-by-two sequential sort on the most 
53:1527:108112:13:13:90:524:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:recent BM and the average GM in the first two fiscal years after the offering year. Then in each 
53:1528:108209:13:12:90:522:393:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:calendar year t, we form four BM-GM portfolios at the beginning of the year across all industry-
53:1529:108305:12:13:90:524:381:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:year IPO cohorts going public in years t-7 to year t-4. We first value-weight stocks within an 
53:1530:108400:13:13:90:525:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:industry-year IPO cohort to form cohort portfolios and then weight cohort portfolios across all 
53:1531:108496:13:12:90:524:355:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:industry-year IPO cohorts by the number of IPOs in each IPO cohort at the end of the third year 
53:1532:108592:12:13:90:525:343:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:after the offering year. The portfolios are rebalanced annually at the beginning of each year. The 
53:1533:108691:13:13:90:525:330:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:second  sub-panel  presents  the  results  of  forming  portfolios  among  all  stocks  in 
53:1534:108782:13:12:90:525:317:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:CRSP/COMPUSTAT in the same industry. First, at the end of each year t, we do a two-by-two 
53:1535:108872:12:13:90:524:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:sequential sort within each industry based on the most recent BM and the average GM in the 
53:1536:108963:13:13:90:522:292:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:previous  two  fiscal  years. Then  we  form  four  BM-GM  portfolios  across  all  industries,  value-
53:1537:109066:13:12:90:524:279:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:weighting  stocks  within  each  industry  to  form  industry  portfolios  and  weighting  industry 
53:1538:109166:12:13:90:524:267:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:portfolios  across  all  industries  by  the  number  of  stocks  in  each  industry,  and  hold  portfolios

56:1635:113117:14:13:90:93:496:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2: 
56:1636:113117:13:14:90:494:483:12:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Note: The sales growth response coefficients are computed using the following regression, 
56:1637:113207:14:14:355:358:469:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f2:                                              
56:1638:113248:14:12:90:525:455:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ExRetq is the industry-adjusted quarterly return over the 3-month period from the end of the first 
56:1639:113347:12:13:90:524:443:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:month of calendar quarter q to the end of the first month of calendar quarter q+1. ΔSGq is the 
56:1640:113442:13:12:90:525:430:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:change in sales growth rate from calendar quarters q-1 to q, where the sales growth rate in quarter 
56:1641:113542:12:13:90:521:418:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:q is calculated as (Salesq - Salesq-4)/ Salesq-4 and Salesq are the sales in quarter q. ΔIBq is the year-
56:1642:113647:13:13:90:525:405:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:over-year change in quarterly earnings, calculated as (IBq -  IBq-4)/ MVq-4, where IBq is the income 
56:1643:113748:13:12:90:524:392:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:before extraordinary items in quarter q and MVq is the market capitalization at the end of quarter 
56:1644:113847:12:13:90:524:380:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:q. ΔCAPXq is the year-over-year change in quarterly capital expenditure, calculated as (CAPXq - 
56:1645:113943:13:13:90:524:367:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:CAPXq-4)/ MVq-4, where CAPXq is the capital expenditure in quarter q. We run the regressions 
56:1646:114036:13:12:90:525:354:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:separately for the low-BM-low-GM group and the low-BM-high-GM group by event years in the 
56:1647:114126:12:13:90:524:342:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:7-year period after event year 0 (the industry IPO wave ending year). We report the sales growth 
56:1648:114223:13:13:90:524:329:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:response coefficient, which is the regression coefficient on ΔSGq, and its t-statistics for both low 
56:1649:114324:13:12:90:525:316:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and high GM growth firms. We also report the difference in the coefficient between high and low 
56:1650:114420:12:13:90:525:304:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:GM groups and its t-statistics. We obtain the industry benchmark of the sales response coefficient 
56:1651:114519:13:13:90:525:291:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:by running the same regression for a sample of all stocks in the same industry as those in industry 
56:1652:114619:13:12:90:525:278:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:IPO waves which were listed at least 3 years before event year 0. All t-statistics are calculated 
56:1653:114717:12:14:90:298:266:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:based on standard errors clustered by industry.

58:1745:116395:19:13:187:506:526:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:t-stat. 1.63 0.34 1.66 2.52 
58:1746:116418:13:12:90:93:513:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2: 
58:1747:116418:12:13:90:525:501:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Note:  This  table  presents  characteristics  of  low-BM  IPO  stocks  by  event  years  in  the  7-year 
58:1748:116524:13:13:90:369:488:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:period after the industry IPO wave ending year (event year 0).  
58:1749:116588:13:12:108:524:475:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Panel A reports the fraction of stocks delisted due to poor performance, as indicated by the 
58:1750:116681:12:13:90:525:463:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:delisting  code  between  500  and  599  in  CRSP.  Panel  B  reports  the  operating  performance 
58:1751:116780:13:13:90:524:450:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:measures including market share and return on assets (ROA). A firm's market share in year t is 
58:1752:116875:13:12:90:524:437:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:calculated as its sales divided by the industry's total sales in year t. A firm's ROA in year t is 
58:1753:116974:12:13:90:524:425:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:calculated as its operating income after depreciation and amortization (OIADP) in year t divided 
58:1754:117071:13:12:90:525:412:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:by the average of total assets (AT) in years t and t-1. For each variable, we report its mean and 
58:1755:117169:12:13:90:525:400:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:standard  deviation  for  low-GM  and  high-GM  growth  firms.  We  also  report  the  difference 
58:1756:117267:13:13:90:525:387:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:between high and low GM groups and its t-statistics. We also report the industry benchmark for 
58:1757:117362:13:12:90:524:374:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:each variable. For each industry IPO wave, we select those stocks in the industry which were 
58:1758:117455:12:13:90:525:362:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:listed at least 3 years before the ending year of the current industry IPO wave, and then take the 
58:1759:117554:13:13:90:524:349:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:mean value of a specific variable among these firms as the industry benchmark for stocks in the 
58:1760:117650:13:12:90:525:336:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:wave. We then weight these industry benchmarks by the number of IPOs in the corresponding 
58:1761:117740:12:13:90:421:324:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:industry IPO waves, and report the weighted mean and standard deviation. 
58:1762:117813:13:13:108:524:311:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Panel C reports the summary statistics of the change in future cash flow forecasts from event 
58:1763:117907:13:12:90:525:298:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:year  3 to  event  year 7.  For  each  BM/GM  group  of  stocks  in  an  industry  IPO  wave,  we first 
58:1764:118011:12:13:90:423:286:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:forecast future cash flows at the end of event year 3 in the following steps.  
58:1765:118090:13:13:108:525:273:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In the first step, we forecast future earnings of the value-weighted portfolio of all stocks in 
58:1766:118186:13:12:90:524:260:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the group based on IBES forecasts of earnings and earnings growth rate. The forecasted earnings 
58:1767:118282:12:13:90:524:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:for the first two years (event years 4 and 5) are taken from IBES consensus (mean) earnings 
58:1768:118374:13:13:90:525:235:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:forecasts. Earnings are then assumed to grow in the next three years (event years 6 to 8) at the 
58:1769:118471:13:12:90:525:222:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:IBES  consensus  (mean)  long-term  growth  rate  forecasts  (LTG).  We  take  the  value-weighted 
58:1770:118570:12:13:90:524:210:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:average of LTGs of all stocks in a portfolio to form the portfolio's LTG. Finally, earnings growth 
58:1771:118669:13:13:90:525:197:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:rate is assumed to converge linearly to a steady growth rate (SGR) in the next 10 years (event 
58:1772:118764:13:12:90:525:184:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:years 9 to 18). We use the median value of all long-term earnings growth rate forecasts in IBES 
58:1773:118860:12:13:90:208:172:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:as the steady growth rate.  
58:1774:118888:13:12:108:525:159:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In the second step, we forecast the book equity values in future years. We first assume a 
58:1775:118978:12:13:90:525:147:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:constant dividend payout ratio (DPR) relative to the cum-dividend book equity value, i.e., Dt = 
58:1776:119074:13:13:90:525:134:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(BEt-1 + Et)*DPR, where Dt is the estimated dividend in year t, BEt-1 is the estimated book equity 
58:1777:119173:13:12:90:524:121:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:value in year t-1, and Et is the estimated earnings in year t. For simplicity, we assume a 5% value 
58:1778:119273:12:13:90:525:109:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:for DPR based on the historical average values of all firms in COMPUSTAT. We then calculate 
58:1779:119365:13:45:90:514:96:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the forecasted book equity values assuming the clean surplus relation, i.e., BEt = BEt-1 + Et - Dt.  
59:1780:119465:45:0:300:315:51:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:58 
59:1781:119468:0:13:108:524:710:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In the third step, we calculate the forecasted ROEs for all future years. Based on forecasted 
59:1782:119562:13:13:90:525:697:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:earnings and book equity values in the next 15 years (event years 4 to 18), we calculate forecasted 
59:1783:119662:13:12:90:524:684:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ROEs in these years, FROEt = Et / BEt-1. Forecasted ROE for all years in the steady state (SROE), 
59:1784:119759:12:13:90:525:672:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:i.e.,  those  years  after  event  year  18,  is  calculated  as  (1+SGR)/(1-DPR)-1,  based  on  the 
59:1785:119860:13:13:90:428:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:equilibrium relationship among these parameters in the steady growth state.  
59:1786:119937:13:13:108:525:646:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In the final step, following Da and Warachka (2009), we form the future cash flow estimate 
59:1787:120028:13:15:90:524:633:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:as  the  discounted  sum  of  all  future  log  ROEs,        ∑                   .  Following 
59:1788:120118:15:13:90:524:618:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Vuolteenaho (2002) and Campbell and Vuolneenaho (2004), we assume a constant value, 0.95, 
59:1789:120208:13:13:90:480:605:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:for , which is estimated from the historical values of market and book dividend yields.  
59:1790:120298:13:13:108:525:592:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:At the end of event year 7, we update the cash flow estimate (ESUM) for each BM/GM group 
59:1791:120387:13:12:90:524:579:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in each industry IPO wave. Forecasted ROEs in event years 4 to 7 are replaced with the realized 
59:1792:120483:12:13:90:524:567:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:values. For all other years after event year 7, the forecasted ROEs are updated, following the 
59:1793:120578:13:12:90:293:554:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:same forecasting procedure described above.  
59:1794:120623:12:13:108:525:542:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We then compute the change in cash flow estimate (∆ESUM) from event year 3 to event year 
59:1795:120712:13:13:90:524:529:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:7 for each BM/GM group in each industry IPO wave. Finally, we use the number of IPOs at the 
59:1796:120804:13:12:90:524:516:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:end  of  event  year  3  in  a wave  to  weight  across  all  industry  IPO  waves  to  estimate  the  final 
59:1797:120913:12:13:90:525:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:statistics of each BM/GM group. We also break down ∆ESUM into three components: ∆ESUM4-7 
59:1798:121001:13:13:90:525:491:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:which is due to errors in short-run forecasted ROEs of event years 4 to 7, ∆ESUM8-12 which is 
59:1799:121095:13:12:90:524:478:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:due to revision in medium-run forecasted ROEs of event years 8 to 12, and ∆ESUM13-inf which is 
59:1800:121190:12:13:90:415:466:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:due to revision in long-run forecasted ROEs of years after event year 13.  
59:1801:121265:13:13:108:525:453:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:For each BM/GM portfolio, we report the weighted mean and the t-statistics for ∆ESUMs. 
59:1802:121352:13:12:90:525:440:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We also report the difference between high and low GM groups and its t-statistics. We also obtain 
59:1803:121450:12:13:90:525:428:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the industry benchmarks of ∆ESUMs in the following steps. First, for each industry IPO wave, 
59:1804:121543:13:13:90:525:415:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:we select all stocks in the same industry as those in the wave which were listed at least 3 years 
59:1805:121641:13:12:90:524:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:before event year 0 to form the value-weighted control portfolio. Second, we estimate ∆ESUMs 
59:1806:121734:12:13:90:525:390:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:for  each  wave  control  portfolio,  following  the  same  procedure  for  the  industry  IPO  wave 
59:1807:121835:13:13:90:524:377:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:portfolios. Finally, we use the number of IPOs at the end of event year 3 in the corresponding 
59:1808:121930:13:12:90:524:364:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:industry IPO wave to weight across all wave control portfolios to estimate the final statistics of 
59:1809:122029:12:13:90:199:352:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the industry benchmark. 
59:1810:122053:13:13:90:93:339:11:Times New Roman:11:Times New Roman:

61:1921:123653:13:12:90:524:318:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Note: Panel A presents the frequency of relevant keywords in the "Risk Factors" section of IPO 
61:1922:123748:12:13:90:525:306:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:prospectuses for portfolios of stocks in industry IPO waves with an offering date after 1994. We 
61:1923:123845:13:13:90:524:293:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:start with those IPOs in our industry IPO wave sample and going public after 1994. The first two 
61:1924:123942:13:12:90:524:280:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:columns report the number of all IPOs in our sample and the number of IPOs with a valid "Risk 
61:1925:124036:12:13:90:524:268:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Factors" section in the IPO prospectus for each BM/GM group. The other columns present the 
61:1926:124127:13:13:90:524:255:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:statistics of the following variables: 1) the count of all words in the IPO prospectus; 2) the count 
61:1927:124228:13:12:90:525:242:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of "Cost(s)" in the IPO prospectus; 3) the percentage of count of "Cost(s)" relative to the total 
61:1928:124326:12:13:90:524:230:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:word count in the IPO prospectus; 4) the count of "Profitability" in the IPO prospectus; 5) the 
61:1929:124422:13:13:90:524:217:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:percentage of count of "Profitability" relative to the total word count in the IPO prospectus. For 
61:1930:124521:13:12:90:525:204:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:each  variable,  we  report  the  mean  and  standard  deviation  for  each  BM/GM  group,  and  the 
61:1931:124622:12:13:90:524:192:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:difference  in  mean  between  high  GM  and  low  GM  groups  within  each  BM  group  and  the 
61:1932:124719:13:13:90:184:179:11:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:associated t-statistic. 
61:1933:124742:13:12:108:525:166:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Panel  B  reports  other  uncertainty  measures  including  the  dispersion  of  analyst  earnings 
61:1934:124841:12:13:90:525:154:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:forecasts and idiosyncratic volatility by event years in the 7-year period after the wave ending 
61:1935:124938:13:12:90:525:141:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:year (event year 0). The dispersion of analyst earnings forecasts for a firm in year t is measured as 
61:1936:125040:12:13:90:525:129:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the average value of the standard deviation of annual earnings per share forecasts reported in 
61:1937:125135:13:13:90:524:116:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:IBES monthly summary file in year t. To estimate a firm's idiosyncratic volatility in year t, we 
61:1938:125232:13:12:90:524:103:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:first regress its daily stock returns in year t on Fama-French three factors (MKTRF, SMB and 
61:1939:125325:12:13:90:525:91:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:HML) and Carhart's momentum factor (UMD), and then calculate the log value of the standard 
61:1940:125416:13:27:90:522:78:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:deviation of the residuals. For each variable, we report its mean and standard deviation for low-
62:1941:125513:27:0:300:315:51:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:61 
62:1942:125516:0:13:90:525:710:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:GM and high-GM growth firms. We also report the difference between high and low GM groups 
62:1943:125606:13:13:90:525:697:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and its t-statistics. We also report the industry benchmark for each variable. For each industry 
62:1944:125703:13:12:90:524:684:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:IPO wave, we select those stocks in the industry which were listed at least 3 years before the 
62:1945:125798:12:13:90:525:672:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ending year of the current industry IPO wave, and then take the mean value of a specific variable 
62:1946:125896:13:13:90:524:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:among  these  firms  as  the  industry  benchmark  for  stocks  in  the  wave.  We  then  weight  these 
62:1947:126000:13:12:90:525:646:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:industry benchmarks by the number of IPOs in the corresponding industry IPO waves, and report 
62:1948:126094:12:14:90:281:634:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the weighted mean and standard deviation.
